<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="26c980bcca3240a89fbedca203d0d83d"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="26c980bcca3240a89fbedca203d0d83d">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'd2411754-ff57-4ce8-92e8-4bff72dac24b'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {

            }

                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else

            <div class="accordion-tabbed"><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Xu/Yang" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a1" data-db-target-for="a1" aria-controls="a1" aria-haspopup="true" id="a1_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Dr. Yang Xu</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a1" aria-labelledby="a1_Ctrl" role="region" id="a1">

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" id="abstract-graphical-en">
         <h2 id="d48101741" class="article-section__header section__title graphical abstractlang_en graphical">Graphical Abstract</h2>
         <div class="graphical-abstract">
            <p><b>The benefits of oxygen vacancies</b> on sodium ion battery performance were demonstrated by using ultrathin Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated MoO<sub>3−<i>x</i></sub> nanosheets as anodes. Owing to the increased electric conductivity and sodium ion diffusion coefficient as well as the reduced solid–electrolyte interphase at deep-discharge conditions, the anodes exhibited high reversible capacity and great rate capability over long-term cycling.
            </p><figure>
               <div class="center graphic__image"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/db443d8a-731b-4428-9af9-b9c8def4b234/mcontent.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/db443d8a-731b-4428-9af9-b9c8def4b234/mcontent.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1051ac38-4deb-4c94-8740-5ff4a11ba7b4/mcontent.gif" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/db443d8a-731b-4428-9af9-b9c8def4b234/mcontent.jpg" alt="Description unavailable" title="Description unavailable" loading="lazy"></picture></a><p class="caption-style"></p>
               </div>
            </figure><p></p>
            </div>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d48101746" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>The utilization of oxygen vacancies (OVs) in sodium ion batteries (SIBs) is expected to enhance performance, but as yet it has rarely been reported. Taking the MoO<sub>3−<i>x</i></sub> nanosheet anode as an example, for the first time we demonstrate the benefits of OVs on SIB performance. Moreover, the benefits at deep-discharge conditions can be further promoted by an ultrathin Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating. A series of measurements show that the OVs increase the electric conductivity and Na-ion diffusion coefficient, and the promotion from ultrathin coating lies in the effective reduction of cycling-induced solid-electrolyte interphase. The coated nanosheets exhibited high reversible capacity and great rate capability with the capacities of 283.9 (50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>) and 179.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (1 A g<sup>−1</sup>) after 100 cycles. This work may not only arouse future attention on OVs for sodium energy storage, but also open up new possibilities for designing strategies to utilize defects in other energy storage systems.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="sec1-bdy-1">
         
         <p>Defects such as oxygen vacancies (OVs) often dominate the electric and chemical properties of transition-metal oxides, and thus they play a crucial role in a wide range of applications.<span><sup><a href="#bib1" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib1_R_d48101733e389" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1">1</a></sup></span> In lithium ion batteries (LIBs), OVs can trigger changes in the electronic structure of metal oxides, so affecting the energetics for electron and ion transport.<span><sup><a href="#bib2" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib2_R_d48101733e392" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Science">2</a></sup></span> Their presence at the electrode/electrolyte interface not only can possibly facilitate the phase transition experienced in lithiation by modified surface thermodynamics, but also well preserve the integrity of the electrode surface morphology.<span><sup><a href="#bib3" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib3_R_d48101733e395" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Phys. Rev. B">3</a></sup></span> The effect of OVs on cyclability and rate capacity has been widely reported in LIBs;<span><sup><a href="#bib4" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib4_R_d48101733e398" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4">4</a></sup></span> however, as far as we know, the relevant study on sodium ion batteries (SIBs) is currently missing. Such kind of knowledge is of great importance to develop the large-scale energy storage devices.</p>
         
         <p>SIBs have recently come again into focus as the important alternative energy storage devices owing to the low cost of Na associated with its natural abundance and decent energy density bestowed by its similar chemical nature to Li. Many electrode materials for LIBs have been investigated as drop-in replacements for SIBs.<span><sup><a href="#bib5" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib5_R_d48101733e404" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5">5</a></sup></span> Owing to the difference in the standard electrochemical potential for Na (3.04 V) and Li (2.71 V), the reduction of voltage can be expected in the Na system when the same chemistry (redox species and host crystal structures) with the Li system is used. The reduction becomes even more significant as Na content in the host structure increases because of the different chemistry from the Na system, for which the larger size of Na-ion (1.02 Å) relative to Li-ion (0.76 Å) is generally believed to be responsible.<span><sup><a href="#bib6" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib6_R_d48101733e407" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6">6</a></sup></span> For example, MoO<sub>3</sub> is generally considered as a LIB cathode but delivers comparable capacity as SIB anode at deep-discharge condition (&lt;0.1 V vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup>).<span><sup><a href="#bib7" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib7_R_d48101733e414" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Electrochem. Commun.">7</a></sup></span> To properly utilize OVs in such a low-voltage system, decomposition of electrolyte (both solvent and salt) and formation of solid–electrolyte interphase (SEI) have to be considered. SEI can largely change the solid–liquid interface, and thus interfere with the function of the OVs, leading to poor coulombic efficiency (CE) and overall capacity loss. It is even more critical for NIBs owing to the higher chemical reactivity of Na over Li.<span><sup><a href="#bib8" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib8_R_d48101733e418" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8">8</a></sup></span> Therefore, using OVs requires combination with other strategy to overcome the adverse effects of SEI and maximize their advantages.</p>
         
         <p>The proper functioning of OVs at the deep-discharge condition requires the reduction of cycling-induced SEI. A thin surface coating by atomic layer deposition (ALD) has proved to be effective regarding the above-mentioned issue.<span><sup><a href="#bib9" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib9_R_d48101733e424" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Mater.">9</a></sup></span> The thin layer can act as a mechanically stable kinetic barrier against electron transfer to the organic carbonate molecules of the electrolytes, thus preventing the formation of excessive amounts of SEI and suppressing the side reactions. Meanwhile, ALD enables a precisely controlled thin coating with pinhole free conformal morphology. A recent work reported that a thin ALD coating of Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> can react with Na-ions to irreversibly form a mechanically durable Na-Al-O layer that acts as an ion transport channel and improves Na-ion diffusion into the electrode through its whole surface.<span><sup><a href="#bib10" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib10_R_d48101733e431" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Nano Lett.">10</a></sup></span> This observation inspires us to use thin Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating as a suitable strategy to ensure the proper functioning of OVs.</p>
         
         <p>In this work, we demonstrate, for the first time, the effect of OVs on sodium energy storage by using MoO<sub>3−<i>x</i></sub> nanosheets as anodes. The nanosheets exhibited improved electrochemical performance comparing to the MoO<sub>3</sub> counterpart owing to the increased electric conductivity and Na-ion diffusion coefficient deriving from the existence of OVs. By coating an ultrathin Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> layer on the electrodes, the function of OVs at the deep-discharge condition was further promoted, giving rise to high reversible capacity and great rate capability over long-term cycling.</p>
         
         <p>The X-ray diffraction (XRD) pattern of the as-prepared nanosheets (Figure <a href="#fig1">1 a</a>) can be assigned to the orthorhombic phase (JCPDS No. 5-0508). Although it is not distinguishable from that of MoO<sub>3</sub> (Supporting Information, Figure S1 a), the exhibited intense blue color (b-Mo hereafter; comparison shown in the inset of Figure <a href="#fig1">1 b</a>) was quite stable in air and can remain unchanged for several months. It changed to white (inset of Figure <a href="#fig1">1 b</a>, w-Mo hereafter) after annealing in air. Both facts strongly indicate the existence of OVs.<span><sup><a href="#bib11" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib11_R_d48101733e466" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. Angew. Chem.">11</a></sup></span> The UV/Vis diffuse reflectance spectroscopy (DRS) spectrum shows strong light absorption in the visible light region (350–700 nm, Figure <a href="#fig1">1 b</a>). Such a blue color originates from the inter-valence charge-transfer transition between Mo<sup>V</sup> and Mo<sup>VI</sup> that coexist in the nanosheets.<span><sup><a href="#bib12" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib12_R_d48101733e477" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12">12</a></sup></span> X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS; Figure <a href="#fig1">1 c</a>; Supporting Information, Figure S2 a) and energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy measurement (EDX; Supporting Information, Figure S2 c) reveal the existence of only Mo and O. The Mo 3d spectrum shows two sets of doublets that are ascribed to Mo<sup>V</sup> and Mo<sup>VI</sup>. The O 1s spectrum provides auxiliary evidence of the OVs, where the peak at 529.8 eV belongs to Mo-O-Mo bonds and the one at 531.1 eV is due to a high number of defect sites with a low oxygen coordination.<span><sup><a href="#bib13" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib13_R_d48101733e488" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13">13</a></sup></span> Scanning electron microscopy (SEM) image (Figure <a href="#fig1">1 d</a>) shows two-dimensional (2D) nanosheets on a large scale with the diameter ranging from 400 nm to 2 μm and thickness of 20–30 nm. Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) image (inset of Figure <a href="#fig1">1 d</a>) confirms the shape of 2D nanosheets, and the HRTEM (Supporting Information, Figure S2 b) image shows clear lattice fringes, verifying the single-crystalline nature of the nanosheets.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="fig1"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/8cd8ba8a-8480-402d-b88b-653df7902c04/mfig001.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/8cd8ba8a-8480-402d-b88b-653df7902c04/mfig001.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/8fe49103-6d76-470a-8475-4b22b592f3d2/mfig001.gif" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/8cd8ba8a-8480-402d-b88b-653df7902c04/mfig001.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=fig1&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201503477" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>a) XRD pattern of the as-prepared MoO<sub>3−<i>x</i></sub> nanosheets. b) UV/Vis DRS spectra of the MoO<sub>3−<i>x</i></sub> and MoO<sub>3</sub> sample with corresponding photographs. c) Mo 3d and O 1s XPS spectra and d) SEM (inset: TEM) image of the sample.</p>
                     </div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>To demonstrate the benefits of OVs, five samples denoted as b-Mo, w-Mo, b-Mo-4Al, b-Mo-8Al, and w-Mo-4Al with the number indicating ALD cycles were tested as SIB anodes based on the existence of OVs and Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating thickness (ca. 1 Å per cycle). EDX elemental mapping on the b-Mo-4Al anode (Supporting Information, Figure S3) clearly shows the uniform Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating on electrode surface. The anodes showed similar cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves (Supporting Information, Figure S4) with a redox pair of 0.71 (anodic)/0.22 V (cathodic) became pronounced after the first cycle, indicating the reversible insertion/extraction of Na ion.<span><sup><a href="#bib7" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib7_R_d48101733e540" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Electrochem. Commun.">7</a></sup></span> However, with the existence of OVs and ultrathin coating, the retention of the anodic peak current is significantly increased (Supporting Information, Figure S4 f). The charge–discharge profiles (Figure <a href="#fig2">2 a</a>; Supporting Information, Figure S4) are in agreement with the corresponding CV results, and the ex situ XRD measurements revealed that the sodiation reaction is an insertion reaction (Supporting Information, Figure S5). Analysis of cycling performance (Figure <a href="#fig2">2 b</a>) and CE (Figure <a href="#fig2">2 c</a>) allows us to draw the following conclusions. 1) With OVs, b-Mo exhibited higher capacities of 254.0 (10th), 139.9 (50th), and 100.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (100th), compared to w-Mo. 2) The coated anodes displayed increased capacities and better retention comparing to their uncoated counterparts. The capacities of 123.9 (w-Mo-4Al), 254.1 (b-Mo-4Al), and 283.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (b-Mo-8Al) were obtained after 100 cycles. A higher CE of the first 20 cycles (&gt;95 % after 5 cycles; inset of Figure <a href="#fig2">2 c</a>) is responsible for the higher capacity and better cyclability. 3) The magnitude of the improvement after coating is more significant with OVs than without OVs, indicating the coating facilitates OV function at the deep-discharge condition. 4) The thickness of Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> can be adjusted to optimize the properties. The b-Mo-8Al anode delivered the capacities of 385.1 (10th), 319.2 (50th), and 283.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (100th) with the CE reaching 95 % after only 4 cycles and remaining over 98 % after 12 cycles. Comparison of rate capability (Figure <a href="#fig2">2 d</a>) shows the same trends as in reversible capacity. Higher capacities were obtained from b-Mo over w-Mo at all rates. Coated anodes delivered higher capacities than their uncoated counterparts and more significant enhancement is achieved with OVs. Among all, b-Mo-8Al exhibited the best rate capability of about 230 (0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and about 180 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). All the results demonstrate the benefits of the OVs that can be further promoted by ultrathin Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating. Compared to w-Mo-4Al, b-Mo delivered higher capacity only at lower rates, which leads us to investigate the coating-promoted benefits of OVs at higher rates.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="fig2"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ec05dbae-d225-452d-93a6-920f0ef72169/mfig002.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/ec05dbae-d225-452d-93a6-920f0ef72169/mfig002.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/416aaee0-b894-4e23-9b0d-b526eb3b3dc5/mfig002.gif" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ec05dbae-d225-452d-93a6-920f0ef72169/mfig002.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=fig2&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201503477" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>a) Charge–discharge profiles of the b-Mo-8Al anode. b) Cycling performance (starting from the second cycle) and c) CE of the anodes at the rate of 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. d) Rate capability in a current density range of 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>–1 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
                     </div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Cycling performance of the anodes with OVs at the rate of 0.2, 0.5 and 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> is shown in Figure <a href="#fig3">3</a>. Without coating, less than 40 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> retained after 100 cycles at all rates. In contrast, the b-Mo-4/8Al anode delivered significantly increased capacities of 216.3/278.5 (0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>), 164.5/225.5 (0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and 123.3/179.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). It is worth noting that similar improvement can be observed from w-Mo-4Al (Supporting Information, Figure S6) but with less prominent capacity increasing without OVs. Such comparison once again confirms the benefits of OVs on cyclability at higher rates. Figure <a href="#fig3">3 d</a> summarizes the CE of three different cycles, where, for the same cycle, it generally decreases with increasing rate. The numbers were substantially improved after coating, which plays a fatal role on the long-term cyclability. More importantly, the coating alleviates the CE reduction caused by increasing rate, which explains the higher capacity retention of the coated anodes at higher rates.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="fig3"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/fd12a87c-4589-4fa4-94d1-43414068117d/mfig003.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/fd12a87c-4589-4fa4-94d1-43414068117d/mfig003.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/78d1867a-9d4d-44a1-a6bc-3b2d09d35959/mfig003.gif" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/fd12a87c-4589-4fa4-94d1-43414068117d/mfig003.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=fig3&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201503477" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Cycling performance of the anodes with OVs at the rate of a) 0.2, b) 0.5, and c) 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. d) Comparison of the CE at different rates.</p>
                     </div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The improved performance of b-Mo over w-Mo can be attributed to the increased electronic conductivity (that is, reduced impedance) and Na-ion diffusion, which can be verified by electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurement. Table <a href="#tbl1" class="scrollableLink">1</a> summarizes the parameters obtained from the Nyquist plots (Supporting Information, Figure S7) before and after 100 cycles at 50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>. Two anodes show similar electrolyte resistance (<i>R</i><sub>s</sub>) due to the same electrolyte. However, b-Mo exhibits much lower charge-transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>), indicating that the electron transport can be significantly improved by OVs during the entire process. After cycling, b-Mo possesses higher Na-ion diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i><sub>Na</sub>) calculated from the low frequency Warburg contribution (Supporting Information, Figure S7 b).<span><sup><a href="#bib14" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib14_R_d48101733e671" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - J. Mater. Chem.">14</a></sup></span> In other words, increased Na-ion diffusion deriving from OVs can be maintained even after long-term cycling.</p>

            <div class="article-section__table-footnotes">
               <ul>
                  <li id="note-p-34">
                     [a] EIS=Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy. <i>R</i><sub>s</sub>=electrolyte resistance, <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>=charge-transfer resistance.

         <p>To illustrate the promoting effect of ultrathin Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating on OVs, EIS and XPS measurements were carried out on the anodes with OVs cycled at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>. As shown in Figure <a href="#fig4">4 a</a> and the Supporting Information, Figure S8, the consistently lower resistance of b-Mo-4/8Al during cycling agrees well with the CE trend and signals lower rates of SEI formation. It demonstrates that Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating effectively improves the kinetics at solid-liquid interface at deep-discharge condition, leading to the higher reversible capacity and better retention at higher rates. XPS results reveal the surface information regarding cycling-induced SEI. In the C 1s (Figure <a href="#fig4">4 b</a>), O 1s (Figure <a href="#fig4">4 c</a>), and Na 2s spectra (Supporting Information, Figure S9), the peaks associated with the electrolyte decomposition products (for example, alkyl, alkoxy, carbonate, ether)<span><sup><a href="#bib15" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib15_R_d48101733e872" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15">15</a></sup></span> show less intensity from the coated anodes. The results support our assumption that Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> layer can act as a mechanically stable substitute for SEI to suppress electrolyte decomposition and inhibit the formation of thick SEI,<span><sup><a href="#bib16" class="bibLink tab-link" id="bib16_R_d48101733e880" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16">16</a></sup></span> thus promoting the function of the OVs at the deep-discharge condition. Moreover, the fact that strong Al signal is still detected after 100 cycles (Figure <a href="#fig4">4 d</a>) confirms that the amount of SEI on the electrode surface is relatively low.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="fig4"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/38eff3fc-ce57-412a-8545-7dea8682c55f/mfig004.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/38eff3fc-ce57-412a-8545-7dea8682c55f/mfig004.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4050cb6f-93f3-434a-a1da-d57123943f18/mfig004.gif" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/38eff3fc-ce57-412a-8545-7dea8682c55f/mfig004.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=fig4&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fanie.201503477" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>a) Comparison of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of the coated anodes during cycling. b) C 1s, c) O 1s, and d) Al 2p XPS spectra of the anodes after 100 cycles at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
                     </div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>In summary, taking ultrathin Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>-coated MoO<sub>3−<i>x</i></sub> nanosheets as example, we have demonstrated the crucial role of OVs in sodium energy storage, which is verified by a series of measurements, including long-term cycling, EIS, and XPS. In detail, OVs can enhance the electric conductivity and Na-ion diffusion coefficient; meanwhile Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> coating can reduce the cycling-induced SEI formation, facilitating the proper functioning of OVs at the deep-discharge condition. Through the combination of OVs and ultrathin surface coating, the b-Mo-8Al anode exhibited high reversible capacity and great rate capability over long-term cycling, delivering capacities of 283.9 (50 mA g<sup>−1</sup>) and 179.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (1 A g<sup>−1</sup>) after 100 cycles. This work aims at providing suitable strategy to take full advantages of OVs in upgrading SIB properties and may open up new possibilities of defects for new energy storage systems.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="sec1">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="sec1-title"> Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <p>Material synthesis and electrode fabrication: MoO<sub>3−<i>x</i></sub> nanosheets were obtained by oxidizing Mo powders in H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> followed by solvothermal treatment in absolute ethanol. Electrodes were fabricated by mixing active material, poly(vinylidenedifluoride) (PVDF), and Super P at a weight ratio of 80:10:10, coated uniformly on Cu foils, and dried at 110 °C under vacuum. Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> was deposited on the as-prepared electrodes using atomic layer deposition. Further experimental details can be found in Supporting Information.</p>
         </section>
